<p><b>Mauricio Macri</b> (<small>Spanish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[mauˈɾisjo ˈmakɾi]</a></span>; born 8 February 1959) is the current <a href="/wiki/President_of_Argentina" title="President of Argentina">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, in office since 2015. A former <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineer</a>, Macri won the first presidential <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">runoff</a> <a href="/wiki/Ballotage_in_Argentina" title="Ballotage in Argentina">ballotage</a> in Argentina's history (the runoff system had been introduced in 1994) and is the first democratically elected non-<a href="/wiki/Radical_Civic_Union" title="Radical Civic Union">Radical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Justicialist_Party" title="Justicialist Party">Peronist</a> President since 1916.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> He was previously the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Mayors_and_Chiefs_of_Government_of_Buenos_Aires" title="List of Mayors and Chiefs of Government of Buenos Aires">Head of Government of the Autonomous City of Buenos Aires</a> from 2007 to 2015 and represented the city of <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Argentina" title="Chamber of Deputies of Argentina">lower house</a> of the Argentine congress from 2005 to 2007.</p>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Tandil" title="Tandil">Tandil</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Buenos Aires Province">Buenos Aires Province</a>, Macri is a graduate of the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Argentina" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina">Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">Bachelor's degree</a> in <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">Civil Engineering</a> and also studied in the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Business_School" title="Columbia Business School">Columbia Business School</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Son of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francesco_Macri" title="Francesco Macri">Francesco Macri</a>, a prominent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> businessman in the industrial and construction sectors, Macri was raised in an <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper class</a> home. He gained recognition when in 1995 he became President of <a href="/wiki/Boca_Juniors" title="Boca Juniors">Boca Juniors</a>, one of the two most popular football clubs in the country. In 2005 he created the <a href="/wiki/Centre-right_politics" title="Centre-right politics">centre-right</a> electoral front <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propuesta_Republicana" title="Propuesta Republicana">Republican Proposal</a> <i>(Propuesta Republicana),</i> also known as PRO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was considered a potential candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_general_election,_2011" title="Argentine general election, 2011">2011 general elections</a>, but declined to run for the presidency of the country and ran instead for reelection as mayor. He got nearly 47% of the vote in the mayoral election, leading to a <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">runoff</a> vote on 31 July 2011 against candidate <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Filmus" title="Daniel Filmus">Daniel Filmus</a>, which he won, getting elected for his second consecutive term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> On 22 November 2015, after a tie in the first round of <a href="/wiki/Argentine_general_election,_2015" title="Argentine general election, 2015">presidential elections on 25 October</a>, he obtained 51.34% of the votes and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_Victory" title="Front for Victory">Front for Victory</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Scioli" title="Daniel Scioli">Daniel Scioli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> He was inaugurated on 10 December 2015 in the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Argentina" title="National Congress of Argentina">National Congress of Argentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, Macri was named one of the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">World's 100 Most Influential People</a> and the Most Powerful President in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> by U.S. news magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Political_views"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Political views</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Syrian_refugees"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Syrian refugees</span></a></li>

</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Cabinet"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Cabinet</span></a></li>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1155" data-file-width="1731" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg/199px-PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg/299px-PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg/398px-PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg 2x" width="199"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PaisajeserranoTandil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri was born in the city of <a href="/wiki/Tandil" title="Tandil">Tandil</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Buenos Aires Province">Buenos Aires Province</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mauricio Macri was born in <a href="/wiki/Tandil" title="Tandil">Tandil</a>, in the province of Buenos Aires, as the son of the Italian-born tycoon <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Macri" title="Francisco Macri">Francisco Macri</a> and Alicia Blanco Villegas, owner of the <a href="/wiki/Philco" title="Philco">Philco</a> brand in Argentina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Villegas_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Villegas-9">[9]</a></sup> The family moved to Buenos Aires a short time later, and kept the houses in Tandil as <a href="/wiki/Holiday_cottage" title="Holiday cottage">vacation properties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Villegas_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Villegas-9">[9]</a></sup> His father influenced him to be a businessman, as well as his uncle Jorge Blanco Villegas. Franco expected Mauricio to eventually succeed him as leaders of his firms. Macri preferred the company of his uncle, to avoid the constant scrutiny of his father. Macri was educated at <a href="/wiki/Colegio_Cardenal_Newman" title="Colegio Cardenal Newman">Colegio Cardenal Newman</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and studied at the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Argentina" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina">Catholic University of Argentina</a> (UCA), where he received a degree in civil engineering. During this time he became interested in <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a>, and joined a <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a> led by the former minister <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Alsogaray" title="Álvaro Alsogaray">Álvaro Alsogaray</a>. As a result, he affiliated to the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Democratic_Centre_(Argentina)" title="Union of the Democratic Centre (Argentina)">Union of the Democratic Centre</a> party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1985, he also attended short courses at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Business_School" title="Columbia Business School">Columbia Business School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania</a> and the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_del_CEMA" title="Universidad del CEMA">Universidad del CEMA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CV_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-CV-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>His professional experience started in SIDECO Americana S.A., a construction company belonging to his father's <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a>, the Socma Group, where he worked for 3 years as Junior Analyst, later becoming a Senior Analyst. In 1984, he worked in the credit department of <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a> Argentina, in Buenos Aires. He joined Socma the same year, and from 1985 onward he served as general manager. In 1992 he became the vice president of <a href="/wiki/Sevel_Argentina" title="Sevel Argentina">Sevel Argentina</a> (then manufacturing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a> automobiles under licence in Argentina, and part of Socma), climbing to the presidency in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CV_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-CV-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991, he was kidnapped for 12 days by officers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Federal_Argentina" title="Policía Federal Argentina">Argentine Federal Police</a>. He was kept inside a very small room, with a chemical bathroom and a hole in the roof to receive food. He was freed after his family reportedly paid a multimillion-dollar ransom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> He has since said that the ordeal led him to decide to enter politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first wife was Ivonne Bordeu, daughter of the racecar driver <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Bordeu" title="Juan Manuel Bordeu">Juan Manuel Bordeu</a>. They had three sons: Agustina, Jimena and Francisco. He got divorced, and married the model <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Isabel_Menditeguy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Isabel Menditeguy (page does not exist)">Isabel Menditeguy</a> in 1994. They signed a <a href="/wiki/Prenuptial_agreement" title="Prenuptial agreement">prenuptial agreement</a>, on Franco's request. The marriage got in crisis when Macri became the chairman of Boca Juniors. They stayed together anyway, but finally divorced in 2005. He started a romance with María Laura Groba, but never got married with her. He left her in 2010, and started a new relation with businesswoman <a href="/wiki/Juliana_Awada" title="Juliana Awada">Juliana Awada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> He got married with Awada that same year. He wore a fake moustache and impersonated singer <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> during the party. He accidentally swallowed the moustache, and Minister of Health <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Lemus" title="Jorge Lemus">Jorge Lemus</a> performed <a href="/wiki/First_aid" title="First aid">first aid</a> to save his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boca_Juniors">Boca Juniors</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg"><img alt="Macri taking part in a friendly match of beach soccer, 2011." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1667" data-file-width="2400" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg/185px-MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg/278px-MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg/370px-MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg 2x" width="185"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MauricioMacrijugandoalfutbol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri playing a friendly match of <a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">beach soccer</a>, 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macri first intended to run for chairman of Boca Juniors in 1991, but his father convinced him to wait and keep working at Sevel. He tried to buy the team <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="Deportivo Español">Deportivo Español</a>, but could not get support from the team's directory. He supported Boca Juniors by paying the wages of the coach <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Luis_Menotti" title="César Luis Menotti">César Luis Menotti</a> and buying players for the team, such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rub%C3%A9n_Perazzo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rubén Perazzo (page does not exist)">Rubén Perazzo</a>. Franco Macri finally allowed his son to try to run Boca Juniors, but suspected that he would fail in it. He instructed his aide <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Orlando_Salvestrini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Orlando Salvestrini (page does not exist)">Orlando Salvestrini</a> to work alongside Mauricio, both to help him and to report his activities. Mauricio Macri met with the former chairmen of Boca Juniors <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Alegre" title="Antonio Alegre">Antonio Alegre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Heller" title="Carlos Heller">Carlos Heller</a>, and tried to convince them to work with him. Heller was confident in his victory and rejected him, as well as Alegre. Later on, he sought the support of other groups within Boca Juniors, eventually winning the internal elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first years were not successful. The performance of the team was poor, the players made frequent complaints over wages and rewards, and he had changed the coach three times. The only initial improvement was a partial reconstruction of the stadium. He arranged that Boca Juniors worked in the stock exchange, to earn enough money to buy new players. His first coach was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Salvador_Bilardo" title="Carlos Salvador Bilardo">Carlos Salvador Bilardo</a>, who brought 14 new players to the team, and ended the tournament in 10th position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> His second coach, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Veira" title="Héctor Veira">Héctor Veira</a>, made a poor performance as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The new coach, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Bianchi" title="Carlos Bianchi">Carlos Bianchi</a>, helped <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rom%C3%A1n_Riquelme" title="Juan Román Riquelme">Juan Román Riquelme</a> to boost his performance, and had <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Palermo" title="Martín Palermo">Martín Palermo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Barros_Schelotto" title="Guillermo Barros Schelotto">Guillermo Barros Schelotto</a> as effective forward players. They won the first two tournaments, going on a record 40-match unbeaten run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_career">Political career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="752" data-file-width="510" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg/220px-Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg/330px-Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg/440px-Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_Foto_de_Prensa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mauricio Macri in 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2003 Macri made his political debut when he founded the centre-right party <a href="/wiki/Commitment_to_Change" title="Commitment to Change">Commitment to Change</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es" xml:lang="es"><i>Compromiso para el Cambio</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-21">[21]</a></sup> The party was conceived as a source for new politicians, as the major parties were discredited after the <a href="/wiki/December_2001_riots_in_Argentina" title="December 2001 riots in Argentina">December 2001 riots in Argentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Later that year he ran for mayor of the City of Buenos Aires for his party. He won the first round of the election with 37%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> but lost the <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">runoff election</a> with 46% of the vote to his opponent <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Ibarra" title="Aníbal Ibarra">Aníbal Ibarra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In 2005, he joined <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_L%C3%B3pez_Murphy" title="Ricardo López Murphy">Ricardo López Murphy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Recreate_for_Growth" title="Recreate for Growth">Recrear</a> to create a political coalition, the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Proposal" title="Republican Proposal">Republican Proposal</a> (PRO) and successfully ran in the City of Buenos Aires for the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Chamber_of_Deputies" title="Argentine Chamber of Deputies">Chamber of Deputies</a>, where he won with 33.9% of the votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> This and later campaigns were managed by <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Dur%C3%A1n_Barba" title="Jaime Durán Barba">Jaime Durán Barba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> A 2007 report mentioned that Macri had attended only 44 of 321 votings. He argued that he became disappointed with the Congress, as the bills sent by the presidency were not open for debate or amendment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Ibarra was impeached and removed from office in 2006, because of the <a href="/wiki/Rep%C3%BAblica_Croma%C3%B1%C3%B3n_nightclub_fire" title="República Cromañón nightclub fire">República Cromañón nightclub fire</a>, and his term of office was completed by his vice, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Telerman" title="Jorge Telerman">Jorge Telerman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout 2006 he alternated his political activities as deputy with his presidency of the soccer club Boca Juniors. In 2007 Macri was in discussions with right-conservative <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Sobisch" title="Jorge Sobisch">Jorge Sobisch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> governor of <a href="/wiki/Neuqu%C3%A9n_Province" title="Neuquén Province">Neuquén Province</a>, ahead of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_Argentina,_2007" title="Elections in Argentina, 2007">2007 national elections</a>. However, this agreement was in conflict with the previous alliance with Ricardo López Murphy, who also intended to run for the presidency and had denounced Sobisch for corruption. Later that year, Sobisch's image was severely damaged when the school teacher Carlos Fuentealba was killed during a union demonstration in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neuqu%C3%A9n,_Argentina" title="Neuquén, Argentina">Neuquén</a>. Facing this situation, Macri immediately backed out of his agreements with Sobisch and remained neutral during the national elections of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The 2007 elections were finally won by <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_Victory" title="Front for Victory">Front for Victory</a> (FPV).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2007 Macri announced that he would run once again for the mayoral elections of the City of Buenos Aires in 2007, heading the PRO slate with <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Michetti" title="Gabriela Michetti">Gabriela Michetti</a> as his running mate. In the <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">first round of the election</a> on 2 June 2007 he won with 45.6% of votes over the government-backed candidate, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Filmus" title="Daniel Filmus">Daniel Filmus</a>, who received 23.8% of the votes. The incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Telerman" title="Jorge Telerman">Jorge Telerman</a>, came in third. The runoff election between Macri and Filmus took place on 24 June 2007, and resulted in Macri's victory with 60.96% of the votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mauricio Macri made an alliance for the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_legislative_election,_2009" title="Argentine legislative election, 2009">2009 midterm elections</a> with <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Narv%C3%A1ez" title="Francisco de Narváez">Francisco de Narváez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Sol%C3%A1" title="Felipe Solá">Felipe Solá</a>. The alliance was successful, as De Narvaez defeated Kirchner in the Buenos Aires province and Gabriela Michetti, Macri's candidate, won the elections in the city of Buenos Aires. Macri was thus considered as a likely candidate to dispute the presidency in the 2011 elections. Cristina Kirchner's public image had a big boost after the <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Death and state funeral of Néstor Kirchner">death and state funeral of Néstor Kirchner</a> in the late 2010, and ran for reelection. Macri ran for his reelection as mayor, instead of the presidency. He won the first rounds of the election on 10 July 2011, with 47.08% of votes against Filmus' 27.78% and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Solanas" title="Fernando Solanas">Fernando "Pino" Solanas</a>, and won the runoff against Filmus again on 31 July, with 64.25% of the votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Buenos_Aires_administration">Buenos Aires administration</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_(8359495338).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2036" data-file-width="1716" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg/200px-Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg/300px-Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg/400px-Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_%288359495338%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_visit%C3%B3_los_talleres-cochera_de_la_Linea_A_de_Subtes_(8359495338).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri visiting the new <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Underground_200_Series" title="Buenos Aires Underground 200 Series">200 Series</a> trains on <a href="/wiki/Line_A_(Buenos_Aires_Underground)" title="Line A (Buenos Aires Underground)">Line A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Underground" title="Buenos Aires Underground">Buenos Aires Underground</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macri's administration did a great deal of work related to public transport, seeking to reduce heavy traffic. One of those works is the <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Buenos_Aires)" title="Metrobus (Buenos Aires)">Metrobus</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit" title="Bus Rapid Transit">Bus Rapid Transit</a> system built in the main avenues of Buenos Aires. By the end of Macri's time as mayor, the system had 5 lines and 113 stations and was 50.5 km (31.4 mi) in total length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other streets have bikeways, to promote the use of bicycles and the city created the <a href="/wiki/EcoBici_(Buenos_Aires)" title="EcoBici (Buenos Aires)">EcoBici</a> bicycle sharing scheme. By the end of Macri's tenure, some 155 km (96 mi) of bicycle lanes were constructed and 49 of the planned 200 automated bicycle sharing stations had been built.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>With regards to rail transport, several level crossings on the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Argentina#Buenos_Aires" title="Rail transport in Argentina">city's commuter rail network</a> have been replaced by tunnels to improve road traffic flow and train frequencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Under Macri's leadership, the city also committed to engage in two large-scale rail infrastructure projects which involve running viaducts through the center of the city in order to extend the <a href="/wiki/Belgrano_Sur_Line" title="Belgrano Sur Line">Belgrano Sur Line</a> and raise the <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_Line" title="San Martín Line">San Martín Line</a> to eliminate level crossings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Macri also presented the <a href="/wiki/Red_de_Expresos_Regionales" title="Red de Expresos Regionales">Red de Expresos Regionales</a> project, which seeks to link the city's main railway termini and railway lines through a series of underground tunnels, though construction will begin during the mandate of <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Larreta" title="Horacio Rodríguez Larreta">Horacio Rodríguez Larreta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Underground" title="Buenos Aires Underground">Buenos Aires Underground</a>, initially maintained by the national government, was the subject of a year long dispute between Macri and Kirchner. The national government sought to transfer it to the city, wich Macri supported, but there were disputed over the budget and the time length of the transition period. Macri finally announced that the city would take control of the underground on November 13, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Line_A_(Buenos_Aires_Underground)" title="Line A (Buenos Aires Underground)">Line A</a>, that still used <a href="/wiki/La_Brugeoise_cars_(Buenos_Aires_Underground)" title="La Brugeoise cars (Buenos Aires Underground)">wooden cars almost a century old</a>, received a renewed fleet of modern cars (paid by the National Government), among other fleet renewals on the network such as new cars for <a href="/wiki/Line_H_(Buenos_Aires_Underground)" title="Line H (Buenos Aires Underground)">Line H</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Among the rolling stock renewals, train purchases for <a href="/wiki/Line_B_(Buenos_Aires_Underground)" title="Line B (Buenos Aires Underground)">Line B</a> were criticised for being bought second-hand from the <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Metro" title="Madrid Metro">Madrid Metro</a>, being technically incompatible with the line and costing more than the <a href="/wiki/CSR_EMU_(Argentina)" title="CSR EMU (Argentina)">new trains for the city's commuter rail network</a>, despite their technical superiority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_police">Metropolitan police</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Metropolitan_Police" title="Buenos Aires Metropolitan Police">Buenos Aires Metropolitan Police</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1781" data-file-width="2500" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg/200px-Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg/300px-Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg/400px-Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri_cadetes_de_la_PM_de_la_CABA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri examining Metropolitan Police graduates</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main police force working in the city at the time was the national police, the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Federal_Police" title="Argentine Federal Police">Argentine Federal Police</a>. Buenos Aires was initially a <a href="/wiki/Federal_district" title="Federal district">federal district</a> with limited autonomy, and became an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_city" title="Autonomous city">autonomous city</a> with the <a href="/wiki/1994_amendment_of_the_Constitution_of_Argentina" title="1994 amendment of the Constitution of Argentina">1994 amendment of the Constitution of Argentina</a>. The police working in the city, however, was still the Federal Police, which depended from the national government instead of the local one. The disputes over a potential transfer of the police were still unresolved when Macri was elected mayor.</p>
<p>Macri tried to negotiate a transfer with president Cristina Kirchner, to no avail. As an alternative, he proposed a bill for the creation of a local police, the <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Metropolitan_Police" title="Buenos Aires Metropolitan Police">Buenos Aires Metropolitan Police</a>, in 2008. This police worked alongside the federal police in the city. The bill was supported by the PRO and the Kirchnerite blocs, and rejected by the blocs of the <a href="/wiki/Civic_Coalition" title="Civic Coalition">Civic Coalition</a> and those aligned with Ibarra. Carrió considered that Macri had declined to continue the transfer request even further, and Ibarra pointed that there would be an overlap of duties between both polices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> It started with nearly 1,000 agents, while the Federal Police had 17,000 agents working in the city. As a result, it only worked with small contraventions, while the most important tasks remained for the Federal police during the transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first chief of the Metropolitan Police, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Alberto_Palacios" title="Jorge Alberto Palacios">Jorge Alberto "Fino" Palacios</a>, was forced to resign on 25 August 2009 after an important public resistance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> due to an ongoing investigation about his involvement in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_AMIA_bombing" title="1994 AMIA bombing">AMIA bombing of 1994</a>. His successor was his second in command, Osvaldo Chamorro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spy_scandal">Spy scandal</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_municipal_spy_scandal" title="Buenos Aires municipal spy scandal">Buenos Aires municipal spy scandal</a></div>
<p>In October 2009, Sergio Burstein, a leader of the Jewish community who had led the opposition against the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Alberto_Palacios" title="Jorge Alberto Palacios">Jorge Alberto Palacios</a> as Chief of Police (because of his connections with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_AMIA_bombing" title="1994 AMIA bombing">terrorist attack on the AMIA</a>), announced in court that he was being spied on by the Police of the City of Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TerraJames_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-TerraJames-50">[50]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, the Chief Justice concluded that Burstein was, in fact, being spied upon by a group that involved Palacios and his successor Osvaldo Palacios Chamorro, a federal police lawyer who worked for the Ministry of Education of Buenos Aires (Ciro James), two judges of the Province of Misiones, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TerraJames_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-TerraJames-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The investigation revealed that the spying included opposition leaders and even leaders from Macri's own party, as well as businessmen, trade unionists, and their families, as the spies had illegally tapped the phone of his brother-in-law, a parapsychologist who had been threatened by Macri's father, industrialist Franco Macri. In December 2009, Fino Palacios, Osvaldo Chamorro and Ciro James were arrested for this incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macri said that the case, headed by judge Norberto Oyarbide, was an attempt by Néstor Kirchner to frame him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Judge <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Casanello" title="Sebastián Casanello">Sebastián Casanello</a> cleared Macri of the charges, ruling that there was not enough evidence of a crime to involve Macri in the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama_Papers_revelations">Panama Papers revelations</span></h3>
<p>In April 2016, following the leak to German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></i> of 11 million documents belonging to Panamanian <a href="/wiki/Law_firm" title="Law firm">law firm</a> <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a>, the leaked <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a> revealed that Macri was <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_named_in_the_Panama_Papers" title="List of people named in the Panama Papers">listed</a> as director of a Bahamas-based trading company that he did not disclose during his tenure as Mayor of Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Shortly after the Panama Papers made the news, Macri appeared in a short TV interview in which he said his father, Franco Macri, had founded the company through a "legal operation". He added that the company had been intended to carry out investment operations in Brazil but the business was never completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Journalist <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Morales_Sol%C3%A1" title="Joaquín Morales Solá">Joaquín Morales Solá</a> considered it unlikely that Macri would be prosecuted for the Panama revelations. Macri appears himself in the directory, Franco Macri had reported it to the AFIP, and it was closed in 2008, just a year after Mauricio Macri became chief of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 7, 2016, federal prosecutor Federico Delgado began a formal investigation into Macri's involvement with Fleg Trading Ltd., the company registered in Panama for which President Macri was listed as director. Judge Sebastián Casanello was asked to start the file on the inquiry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The initial petition was made by Norman Martínez, deputee for the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_Victory" title="Front for Victory">Front for Victory</a>. Martínez claims Macri could be guilty of perjury due to omissions made in his sworn statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Martínez also referenced another offshore company, Kagemusha SA, which had been established in 1981 and to which President Macri also had connections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_elections">Presidential elections</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Argentine_general_election,_2015" title="Argentine general election, 2015">Argentine general election, 2015</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Presidential_debates_in_Argentina" title="Presidential debates in Argentina">Presidential debates in Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ballotage_in_Argentina" title="Ballotage in Argentina">Ballotage in Argentina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri-Presidente.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="800" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macri-Presidente.png/200px-Macri-Presidente.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macri-Presidente.png/300px-Macri-Presidente.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Macri-Presidente.png/400px-Macri-Presidente.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri-Presidente.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri's 2015 presidential campaign logo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macri ran for president of Argentina in the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_general_election,_2015" title="Argentine general election, 2015">2015 presidential elections</a>. As President Cristina Kirchner was unable to run, initial opinion polls revealed a three-way tie among Macri, the <a href="/wiki/Kirchnerism" title="Kirchnerism">Kirchnerite</a> governor <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Scioli" title="Daniel Scioli">Daniel Scioli</a>, and the mayor of <a href="/wiki/Tigre,_Buenos_Aires" title="Tigre, Buenos Aires">Tigre</a> <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Massa" title="Sergio Massa">Sergio Massa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Failing to achieve enough support, the <a href="/wiki/Broad_Front_UNEN" title="Broad Front UNEN">Broad Front UNEN</a> coalition disbanded, and <a href="/wiki/Elisa_Carri%C3%B3" title="Elisa Carrió">Elisa Carrió</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Civic_Union" title="Radical Civic Union">Radical Civic Union</a> created a new coalition with the Republican Proposal, forming <a href="/wiki/Cambiemos" title="Cambiemos">Cambiemos</a>. He supported <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Larreta" title="Horacio Rodríguez Larreta">Horacio Rodríguez Larreta</a> against Gabriela Michetti in the primary elections of PRO for the position of mayor of Buenos Aires. Larreta won both the primary and the main elections, and Michetti was selected as candidate for the vice-presidency. Macri also declined an electoral alliance with Massa, and kept <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Eugenia_Vidal" title="María Eugenia Vidal">María Eugenia Vidal</a> as candidate for governor of the Buenos Aires province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macri, Carrió and <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Sanz" title="Ernesto Sanz">Ernesto Sanz</a> ran in the primary elections, which Macri won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Opinion polls previous to the result suggested that Scioli would win by a wide margin, and might even be able to avoid a <a href="/wiki/Ballotage_in_Argentina" title="Ballotage in Argentina">ballotage</a>. However, the final results showed only a narrow lead for Scioli, with his 37.08% just ahead of Macri's 34.15%, leading to new elections on 22 November. Massa got the third place, with 21% of the vote, and both candidates sought to secure the voters that had voted for him. Both candidates were polarized on the opinion about the presidency of Cristina Kirchner: Scioli proposes to keep most of the Kirchnerite policies, and Macri to change them. In the legislative elections, the FPV lost the majority of the chamber of deputies, but keeps the majority of the senate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scioli declined to attend the first <a href="/wiki/Presidential_debates_in_Argentina" title="Presidential debates in Argentina">leaders' debate</a> previous to the elections, which was held between the other five candidates instead. When the ballotage was confirmed, he asked Macri for a presidential debate between both candidates, which was accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Two debates were being organized: one by the NGO "Argentina debate", and another one by the TV news channel <a href="/wiki/Todo_Noticias" title="Todo Noticias">Todo Noticias</a>. Macri preferred to take part in a single debate with Scioli, and opted for the one organized by Argentina Debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macri criticized Scioli for a <a href="/wiki/Negative_campaigning" title="Negative campaigning">negative campaigning</a> launched by the Front for Victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Several politicians and state institutions run by the FPV released messages warning about terrible things that may happen if Macri was elected president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Scioli claims that it was a campaign to encourage public awareness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> It is rumored that the campaign may been suggested by the Brazilian <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jo%C3%A3o_Santana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="João Santana (page does not exist)">João Santana</a>, who organized a similar one in Brazil during the ballotage of <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> and <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9cio_Neves" title="Aécio Neves">Aécio Neves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ballotage was held on November 22. Daniel Scioli accepted his defeat when 70% of the votes were counted; the provisional results were 53% and 47% at that moment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The distance between both candidates slowly reduced in the following hours, leading to a victory of a smaller margin for Macri than most exit polls suggested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Nevertheless, his victory has ended the 12-year rule of <a href="/wiki/Kirchnerism" title="Kirchnerism">Kirchnerism</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Days after the election, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> telephoned Macri to congratulate him on the results. According to the <a href="/wiki/White_House_Press_Secretary" title="White House Press Secretary">White House press release</a>, President Obama "emphasized the longstanding partnership between the United States and Argentina and conveyed his commitment to deepen cooperation on multilateral issues, improve commercial ties, and expand opportunities in the energy sector."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency">Presidency</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Mauricio_Macri" title="Presidency of Mauricio Macri">Presidency of Mauricio Macri</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President-elect">President-elect</span></h3>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-weight: normal; background-color: #DEDEDE;"><span style="font-size:80%">Presidential styles of</span><br/>
<b><span class="fn">Mauricio Macri</span></b></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg"><img alt="Standard of the President of Argentina.svg" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg/75px-Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg/113px-Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg/150px-Standard_of_the_President_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" width="75"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">Reference style</a></th>
<td><i><span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">Excelentísimo Señor Presidente de la Nación</span></i><br/>
"His Most Excellent Mister President of the Nation"</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Spoken style</th>
<td><i><span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">Presidente de la Nación</span></i><br/>
"President of the Nation"</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Alternative style</th>
<td><i><span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">Señor Presidente</span></i><br/>
"Mister President"</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>He has promised to reduce inflation, improve conditions for business, and cease the international alignment with Venezuela and Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Macri has announced an <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> development strategy named <i>Plan Belgrano</i> (after <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Belgrano" title="Manuel Belgrano">Manuel Belgrano</a>), a plan aimed at building infrastructure and encouraging industry development in ten of Argentina's northern <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Argentina" title="Provinces of Argentina">provinces</a>, which have historically lagged behind the rest of the country. The plan includes a proposed investment equivalent to 16 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_dollars" title="United States dollars">United States dollars</a> over the course of 10 years, along with an "historical reconstruction fund" of 50 billion <a href="/wiki/Argentine_peso" title="Argentine peso">pesos</a> to be used in 4 years. Other objectives of the plan include the provision of <a href="/wiki/Housing" title="Housing">housing</a> for some 250,000 families, and the construction of 1400 <a href="/wiki/Child_care" title="Child care">child care</a> centers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macri announced the full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Mauricio_Macri" title="Cabinet of Mauricio Macri">composition of his cabinet</a> on November 25, 2015, some two weeks before he was due to take office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The period of <a href="/wiki/Argentina_presidential_transition" title="Argentina presidential transition">presidential transition</a> proved to be particularly conflictive. Both presidents had a very short meeting, where Cristina refused to provide any help or insight for Macri's future administration, and only accepted to talk about the ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Mauricio Macri took office on 10 December 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inauguration">Inauguration</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_Mauricio_Macri" title="Inauguration of Mauricio Macri">Inauguration of Mauricio Macri</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1515" data-file-width="2000" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg/220px-Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg/330px-Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg/440px-Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri_recibi%C3%B3_el_bast%C3%B3n_y_la_banda_presidencial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri receiving the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_sash" title="Presidential sash">presidential sash</a> at <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosada" title="Casa Rosada">Casa Rosada</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macri took office on 10 December 2015. He began the ceremony starting from his apartment in the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Recoleta,_Buenos_Aires" title="Recoleta, Buenos Aires">Recoleta</a> at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Avenida_del_Libertador" title="Avenida del Libertador">Avenida del Libertador</a> and Cavia at 11:00pm to the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Argentina" title="National Congress of Argentina">National Congress of Argentina</a> with his wife <a href="/wiki/Juliana_Awada" title="Juliana Awada">Juliana Awada</a> and his youngest daughter of 4 years old, through the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosada" title="Casa Rosada">Casa Rosada</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Mayo" title="Plaza de Mayo">Plaza de Mayo</a>. At 11:41 he entered the room where the Legislature was, taking an oath after the Vice President <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Michetti" title="Gabriela Michetti">Gabriela Michetti</a>. Then he delivered a speech of 27 minutes in which he pledged his "support for an independent judiciary, to fight corruption and drug trafficking, the internal union of Argentina, universal social protection, create a XXI-century style of education and that everyone can have a roof, water and sewer". He also greeted those who were his competitors during the presidential elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg/220px-Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg/330px-Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg/440px-Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gabinete_de_Mauricio_Macri.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri with his cabinet in the <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museo_Casa_Rosada" title="es:Museo Casa Rosada">Casa Rosada Museum</a>, 10 December 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Later he went to the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosada" title="Casa Rosada">Casa Rosada</a>, where he received the presidential attributes in the White Hall at the hands of the Temporary President of the Senate, <a href="/wiki/Federico_Pinedo" title="Federico Pinedo">Federico Pinedo</a>, accompanied by Vice President <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Michetti" title="Gabriela Michetti">Gabriela Michetti</a>, President of the Chamber of Deputies Emilio Monzó and President of the Supreme Court <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lorenzetti" title="Ricardo Lorenzetti">Ricardo Lorenzetti</a>. Minutes later he went to the historic balcony where thousands of people waited in the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Mayo" title="Plaza de Mayo">Plaza de Mayo</a>, expressing his hope that "Argentines deserve to live better and we are about to start a wonderful period for our country. I promise to be always telling the truth, and showing where our problems are" and calling "all the Argentines to accompany his administration and alert them when [the government] makes mistakes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>After being anointed President, he gave a reception at the <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_Palace" title="San Martín Palace">San Martín Palace</a> of Argentina Foreign Ministry to all the heads of state present: <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a> from <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Juan_Carlos_I" title="King Juan Carlos I">King Juan Carlos I</a> of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and representatives of other countries attending his inauguration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Argentina" title="Foreign relations of Argentina">Foreign relations of Argentina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_presidential_trips_made_by_Mauricio_Macri" title="List of presidential trips made by Mauricio Macri">List of presidential trips made by Mauricio Macri</a></div>
<p>During his government, Macri wants to strengthen ties with <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a>, looking away from the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarianism" title="Bolivarianism">Bolivarian</a> axis and claim for political prisoners in <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. It will also promote the repeal of the agreement with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and work for a rapprochement with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> He has also worked to strengthen relations with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2992" data-file-width="4000" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png/225px-Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png/338px-Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png/450px-Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_2.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri with Mexican President <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosada" title="Casa Rosada">Casa Rosada</a>. Argentina and Mexico, along with Brazil are the most developed economies in Latin America, and members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G20_major_economies" title="G20 major economies">G20 major economies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After being elected President, Macri received many congratulations from other Latin American Presidents. Despite the ruling <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_(Brazil)" title="Workers' Party (Brazil)">Workers' party</a> having supported <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Scioli" title="Daniel Scioli">Daniel Scioli</a> during the campaign, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">Brazilian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> congratulated Macri and invited him to a state visit "as soon as possible", while she was also set to attend <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_Mauricio_Macri" title="Inauguration of Mauricio Macri">Macri's inauguration</a> as president. The pair have favored improving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentina-Brazil_relations" title="Argentina-Brazil relations">bilateral relations</a> between the two countries, as well as strengthening the <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> trade bloc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Armendariz_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Armendariz-98">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Chile" title="President of Chile">Chilean President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a>, contacted Macri by phone and spoke about the importance for both countries of maintaining the spirit of cooperation, integration and development which characterizes their common history and the importance of further work for <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> expressed "Congratulations to Mauricio Macri for his victory in presidential elections in Argentina. Successes in his management. It has our full support".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ecuador" title="President of Ecuador">President of Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a>, congratulated Macri for his victory and wished him "the best of luck". While commenting on the presidencies of the <a href="/wiki/Kirchnerism" title="Kirchnerism">Kirchners</a>, he stated that "12 years ago Argentina was reborn like a phoenix, after <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a> had left it in ashes" whilst thanking the former President <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">President of Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a>, stated that "Mexico will work with" Macri's government to strengthen "bilateral relations and the wellbeing of Latin America".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlianzadelPacifico_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-AlianzadelPacifico-102">[102]</a></sup> Peruvian President <a href="/wiki/Ollanta_Humala" title="Ollanta Humala">Ollanta Humala</a> contacted Macri in order to congratulate him on his election victory and point out that the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Peru" title="Government of Peru">Peruvian Government</a> has "strong will" to strengthen ties with his country, reported the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Relations_(Peru)" title="Ministry of Foreign Relations (Peru)">Peruvian Foreign Ministry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Uruguayan president <a href="/wiki/Tabar%C3%A9_V%C3%A1zquez" title="Tabaré Vázquez">Tabaré Vázquez</a> greeted Macri by telephone and asked him to convey his congratulations to the people of Argentina for the civic maturity demonstrated during the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri_Temer_7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2707" data-file-width="4000" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Macri_Temer_7.jpg/225px-Macri_Temer_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Macri_Temer_7.jpg/338px-Macri_Temer_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Macri_Temer_7.jpg/450px-Macri_Temer_7.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri_Temer_7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri with Brazilian President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Quinta_de_Olivos" title="Quinta de Olivos">Quinta de Olivos</a>. Brazil is Argentina's biggest trade partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Immediately after the elections, Macri announced that he would ask for the invocation of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>'s "democratic clause" (limiting membership to democracies) with regard to <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, since the government of <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Maduro" title="Nicolás Maduro">Nicolás Maduro</a> was not respecting democratic doctrines. He called for the holding of the <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_parliamentary_election,_2015" title="Venezuelan parliamentary election, 2015">2015 Venezuelan elections</a> without electoral fraud or tricks to avoid the result, and the release of political prisoners. In the end Maduro acknowledged the defeat of his party in the elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Macri made diplomatic requests for the political prisoners in the first meeting of Mercosur that he attended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unity_Roundtable" title="Democratic Unity Roundtable">opposition</a> hailed Macri's presidential win in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> as a blow for leftists in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and a good omen for their own duel with <i><a href="/wiki/Chavism" title="Chavism">Chavism</a></i> in the next month's <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_parliamentary_election,_2015" title="Venezuelan parliamentary election, 2015">parliamentary vote</a>. "That was a big disappointment for Venezuela's ruling socialist 'Chavismo' movement, which had a close political alliance with Fernández."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diosdado_Cabello" title="Diosdado Cabello">Diosdado Cabello</a> called Macri a "<a href="/wiki/Fascist_(insult)" title="Fascist (insult)">fascist</a>", and asked him to stay away from Venezuelan internal affairs, as Macri had proposed to remove Venezuela from the Mercosur because of the treatment to <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_L%C3%B3pez" title="Leopoldo López">Leopoldo López</a> and other political prisoners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The victory of Macri is considered part of the decline of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pink_Tide" title="Pink Tide">Pink Tide</a> in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 5, Macri made his first trip as President-elect to <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, where he met with President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brasilia" title="Brasilia">Brasilia</a>. Macri said he chose <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> for his first trip as President-elect because it is the main commercial partner of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and because of the strong ties that both countries have.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> That same day, Mauricio Macri traveled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" title="Santiago de Chile">Santiago de Chile</a>, where he was received by President <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_de_la_Moneda" title="Palacio de la Moneda">Palacio de la Moneda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1906" data-file-width="2085" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg/338px-Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Macri_with_Barack_Obama_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President Macri with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, during his official visit to Argentina, March 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> congratulated the country for its "successful elections", adding that he was "looking forward to working closely" with Macri and his government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Argentina" title="United States Ambassador to Argentina">United States Ambassador to Argentina</a> <a href="/wiki/Noah_Mamet" title="Noah Mamet">Noah Mamet</a> wished Macri well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlianzadelPacifico_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-AlianzadelPacifico-102">[102]</a></sup> Members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> later asked <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in a letter to prioritise US-Argentine relations during 2016, stating that "The United States and Argentina should be natural partners. Both have highly educated populations, diversified economies and vast natural resources" and calling such a relationship a "win-win" for both countries. The letter also stressed the importance of reversing high levels of <a href="/wiki/Anti-Americanism" title="Anti-Americanism">anti-Americanism</a> in the country and resolving the holdout problem with the <a href="/wiki/Vulture_fund" title="Vulture fund">vulture funds</a>, among other key issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Obama later congratulated Macri personally, while an official <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> statement confirmed that the President intends to strengthen ties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentina-United_States_relations" title="Argentina-United States relations">relations between Argentina and the United States</a> began to twitch due to the problem that came into the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Argentina" title="Government of Argentina">Argentine Government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vulture_fund" title="Vulture fund">vulture fund</a>, where former President <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a> stated after the latter denial of certiorari that her country had an obligation to pay its creditors, but not to become the victims of <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">extortion</a> by speculators; even if Argentina can't use the U.S. financial system to do so, she said, teams of experts are working on ways to avoid such a default and keep Argentina's promises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The expiration of Rights Upon Future Offers (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RUFO" title="RUFO">RUFO</a>) in December 2014 will preclude other bondholders from suing for better terms should the Argentine Government and the vulture funds settle, making such a settlement all the more likely after that date, should the dispute continue.</p>
<p>On February 18, 2016, a <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> official announced that President Obama would undertake a state visit to Argentina on March 23–24, 2016 to improve the <a href="/wiki/Argentina%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Argentina–United States relations">Argentina–United States relations</a> after the two countries' relations under predecessors <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a> and <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a> saw tension in trade and investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> President Obama and the First Family arrived in Buenos Aires <a href="/wiki/Ministro_Pistarini_International_Airport" title="Ministro Pistarini International Airport">Ministro Pistarini International Airport</a> from Havana, Cuba at around 1 a.m. (<a href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%9203:00" title="UTC−03:00">UTC−3</a>) on Wednesday, March 23, where they were greeted by <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_and_Worship" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Worship">Argentine Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Susana_Malcorra" title="Susana Malcorra">Susana Malcorra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Obama and Macri discussed ways to strengthen cooperation in promoting "<a href="/wiki/Universal_value" title="Universal value">universal values</a> and interests," such as in the areas of security, energy, health and human rights, where the two presidents have agreed for <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_agencies_in_the_United_States" title="List of federal agencies in the United States">U.S. federal agencies</a> to assist <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Argentina#Responses_and_counterterrorism_efforts" title="Terrorism in Argentina">Argentina's counter-terrorism efforts</a>, to contribute to <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> missions, combat <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">illegal drug trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a>, respond to diseases and <a href="/wiki/Outbreak" title="Outbreak">outbreaks</a> like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zika_virus_outbreak_(2015%E2%80%93present)" title="Zika virus outbreak (2015–present)">Zika virus</a>, and develop resources and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> strategies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Obama also praised Macri for his economic reforms that helped create "sustainable and <a href="/wiki/Inclusive_growth" title="Inclusive growth">inclusive</a> <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>" and "reconnected Argentina with the <a href="/wiki/World_economy" title="World economy">world economy</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Thus, Obama declared a "fresh era" of relations that would help Argentina's credibility in the Latin American region and the world, and announced trade and economic initiatives to reset the countries relations after years of tension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 March 2016, Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Susana_Malcorra" title="Susana Malcorra">Susana Malcorra</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> signed agreements with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> to join again on the <a href="/wiki/Visa_Waiver_Program" title="Visa Waiver Program">Visa Waiver Program</a>. Argentina initially joined on the program in 1996, but was removed in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macri_and_Merkel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1663" data-file-width="2500" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Macri_and_Merkel.jpg/210px-Macri_and_Merkel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Macri_and_Merkel.jpg/315px-Macri_and_Merkel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Macri_and_Merkel.jpg/420px-Macri_and_Merkel.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macri_and_Merkel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macri with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Chancellor" title="German Chancellor">German Chancellor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, during his European tour, July 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many European leaders publicly expressed support for the new government of Macri. <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> congratulated Macri and requested that he make a state visit to <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. She added that the two countries have "always been deeply tied", particularly in the area of science, which she deemed "one of the pillars" of the two countries' relations.
